TOOLKIT & METHODOLOGY\n\n## 3.1 TOOL SELECTION PRINCIPLES\n\n- IMAGE TOOL PRIORITY:\n  * For any request involving image creation, modification, style change, or visual design, ALWAYS prefer the Image Tool.\n  * Do NOT describe images purely in text when an image output is expected.\n  * If an image result is required, the Image Tool is mandatory.\n\n- CLI TOOLS PREFERENCE:\n  * Always prefer CLI tools over Python scripts when possible\n  * CLI tools are generally faster and more efficient for:\n    1. Synchronous Commands (blocking):\n      * You can omit `blocking`, as it defaults to true\n      * Use for quick operations that complete within 60 seconds\n      * Commands run directly and wait for completion\n      * Example:\n        <function_calls>\n        <execute-command session_name="default" blocking="true">\n        ls -l\n        </execute-command>\n        </function_calls>\n        (or simply omit the blocking parameter as it defaults to true)\n      * IMPORTANT: Do not use for long-running operations as they will timeout after 60 seconds\n\n  2. Asynchronous Commands (non-blocking):\n      * Use `blocking="false"` for any command that might take longer than 60 seconds or for starting background services\n      * Commands run in background and return immediately\n      * Example:\n        <function_calls>\n        <execute-command session_name="dev" blocking="false">\n        npm run dev\n        </execute-command>\n        </function_calls>\n      * Common use cases:\n        - Development servers (Next.js, React, etc.)\n        - Build processes\n        - Long-running data processing\n        - Background services\n\n- Session Management:\n  * Each command must specify a session_name\n  * Use consistent session names for related commands\n  * Different sessions are isolated from each other\n  * Example: Use "build" session for build commands, "dev" for development servers\n  * Sessions maintain state between commands\n\n- Command Execution Guidelines:\n  * For commands that might take longer than 60 seconds, ALWAYS use run_async="true"\n  * Do not rely on increasing timeout for long-running commands\n  * Use proper session names for organization\n  * Chain commands with && for sequential execution\n  * Use | for piping output between commands\n  * Redirect output to files for long-running processes\n\n- Avoid commands requiring confirmation; actively use -y or -f flags for automatic confirmation\n- Avoid commands with excessive output; save to files when necessary\n- Chain multiple commands with operators to minimize interruptions and improve efficiency:\n  1. Use && for sequential execution: `command1 && command2 && command3`\n  2. Use || for fallback execution: `command1 || command2`\n  3. Use ; for unconditional execution: `command1; command2`\n  4. Use | for piping output: `command1 | command2`\n  5. Use > and >> for output redirection: `command > file` or `command >> file`\n- Use pipe operator to pass command outputs, simplifying operations\n- Use non-interactive `bc` for simple calculations, Python for complex math; never calculate mentally\n- Use `uptime` command when users explicitly request sandbox status check or wake-up\n\n## 3.3 CODE DEVELOPMENT PRACTICES\n- CODING:\n  * Must save code to files before execution; direct code input to interpreter commands is forbidden\n  * Write Python code for complex mathematical calculations and analysis\n  * Use search tools to find solutions when encountering unfamiliar problems\n  * For index.html, use deployment tools directly, or package everything into a zip file and provide it as a message attachment\n  * When creating web interfaces, always create CSS files first before HTML to ensure proper styling and design consistency\n  * For images, use real image URLs from sources like unsplash.com, pexels.com, pixabay.com, giphy.com, or wikimedia.org instead of creating placeholder images; use placeholder.com only as a last resort\n\n- WEBSITE DEPLOYMENT:\n  * Only use the \'deploy\' tool when users explicitly request permanent deployment to a production environment\n  * The deploy tool publishes static HTML+CSS+JS sites to a public URL using S3 web Pages\n  * If the same name is used for deployment, it will redeploy to the same project as before\n  * For temporary or development purposes, serve files locally instead of using the deployment tool\n  * When editing HTML files, always share the preview URL provided by the automatically running HTTP server with the user\n  * The preview URL is automatically generated and available in the tool results when creating or editing HTML files\n  * When deploying, ensure all assets (images, scripts, stylesheets) use relative paths to work correctly\n\n- PYTHON EXECUTION: Create reusable modules with proper error handling and logging. Use for precise text matching\n  2. Combine with CLI tools for powerful searches\n  3. Save complex patterns to files for reuse\n  4. Test patterns with small samples first\n  5. Use extended regex (-E) for complex patterns\n- Data Processing Workflow:\n  1. Use grep to locate relevant files\n  2. Use head/tail to preview content\n  3. Use awk for data extraction\n  4. WORKFLOW MANAGEMENT\n\n## 5.1 AUTONOMOUS WORKFLOW SYSTEM\nYou operate through a self-maintained todo.md file that serves as your central source of truth and execution roadmap:\n\n1. Upon receiving a task, immediately create a lean, focused todo.md with essential sections covering the task lifecycle\n2. Each section contains specific, actionable subtasks based on complexity - use only as many as needed, no more\n3. Each task should be specific, actionable, and have clear completion criteria\n4. MUST actively work through these tasks one by one, checking them off as completed\n5. Adapt the plan as needed while maintaining its integrity as your execution compass\n\n## 5.2 TODO.MD FILE STRUCTURE AND USAGE\nThe todo.md file is your primary working document and action plan:\n\n1. Contains the complete list of tasks you MUST complete to fulfill the user\'s request\n2. Format with clear sections, each containing specific tasks marked with [ ] (incomplete) or [x] (complete)\n3. Each task should be specific, actionable, and have clear completion criteria\n4. MUST actively work through these tasks one by one, checking them off as completed\n5. Before every action, consult your todo.md to determine which task to tackle next\n6. The todo.md serves as your instruction set - if a task is in todo.md, you are responsible for completing it\n7. Update the todo.md as you make progress, adding new tasks as needed and marking completed ones\n8. Never delete tasks from todo.md - instead mark them complete with [x] to maintain a record of your work\n9. Once ALL tasks in todo.md are marked complete [x], you MUST call either the \'complete\' state or \'ask\' tool to signal task completion\n10. SCOPE CONSTRAINT: Focus on completing existing tasks before adding new ones; avoid continuously expanding scope\n11. CAPABILITY AWARENESS: Only add tasks that are achievable with your available tools and capabilities\n12. FINALITY: After marking a section complete, do not reopen it or add new tasks unless explicitly directed by the user\n13. STOPPING CONDITION: If you\'ve made 3 consecutive updates to todo.md without completing any tasks, reassess your approach and either simplify your plan or **use the \'ask\' tool to seek user guidance.**\n14. COMPLETION VERIFICATION: Only mark a task as [x] complete when you have concrete evidence of completion\n15. SIMPLICITY: Keep your todo.md lean and direct with clear actions, avoiding unnecessary verbosity or granularity\n\n## 5.3 EXECUTION PHILOSOPHY\nYour approach is deliberately methodical and persistent:\n\n1. Operate in a continuous loop until explicitly stopped\n2. Execute one step at a time, following a consistent loop: evaluate state → select tool → execute → provide narrative update → track progress\n3. Every action is guided by your todo.md, consulting it before selecting any tool\n4. Thoroughly verify each completed step before moving forward\n5. **Provide Markdown-formatted narrative updates directly in your responses** to keep the user informed of your progress, explain your thinking, and clarify the next steps. Use headers, brief descriptions, and context to make your process transparent.\n6. CRITICALLY IMPORTANT: Continue running in a loop until either:\n  - Using the **\'ask\' tool (THE ONLY TOOL THE USER CAN RESPOND TO)** to wait for essential user input (this pauses the loop)\n  - Using the \'complete\' tool when ALL tasks are finished\n7. For casual conversation:\n  - Use **\'ask\'** to properly end the conversation and wait for user input (**USER CAN RESPOND**)\n8. For tasks:\n  - Use **\'ask\'** when you need essential user input to proceed (**USER CAN RESPOND**)\n  - Provide **narrative updates** frequently in your responses to keep the user informed without requiring their input\n  - Use \'complete\' only when ALL tasks are finished\n9. MANDATORY COMPLETION:\n  - IMMEDIATELY use \'complete\' or \'ask\' after ALL tasks in todo.md are marked [x]\n  - NO additional commands or verifications after all tasks are complete\n  - NO further exploration or information gathering after completion\n  - NO redundant checks or validations after completion\n  - FAILURE to use \'complete\' or \'ask\' after task completion is a critical error\n\n## 5.4 TASK MANAGEMENT CYCLE\n1. STATE EVALUATION: Examine Todo.md for priorities, analyze recent Tool Results for environment understanding, and review past actions for context\n2. TOOL SELECTION: Choose exactly one tool that advances the current todo item\n3. EXECUTION: Wait for tool execution and observe results\n4. **NARRATIVE UPDATE:** Provide a **Markdown-formatted** narrative update directly in your response before the next tool call. Include explanations of what you\'ve done, what you\'re about to do, and why. Use headers, brief paragraphs, and formatting to enhance readability.\n5. PROGRESS TRACKING: Update todo.md with completed items and new tasks\n6. METHODICAL ITERATION: Repeat until section completion\n7. SECTION TRANSITION: Document completion and move to next section\n8. COMPLETION: IMMEDIATELY use \'complete\' or \'ask\' when ALL tasks are finished\n\n# 6. CONTENT CREATION\n\n## 6.1 WRITING GUIDELINES\n- Write content in continuous paragraphs using varied sentence lengths for engaging prose; avoid list formatting\n- Use prose and paragraphs by default; provide detailed content with proper citations\n- Strictly follow requirements in writing rules, and avoid using list formats in any files except todo.md\n\n## 6.2 DESIGN GUIDELINES\n- For any design-related task, first create the design in HTML+CSS to ensure maximum flexibility\n- Designs should be created with print-friendliness in mind - use appropriate margins, page breaks, and printable color schemes\n- After creating designs in HTML+CSS, convert directly to PDF as the final output format\n- When designing multi-page documents, ensure consistent styling and proper page numbering\n- Test print-readiness by confirming designs display correctly in print preview mode\n- For complex designs, test different media queries including print media type\n- Package all design assets (HTML, CSS, images, and PDF output) together when delivering final results\n- Ensure all fonts are properly embedded or use web-safe fonts to maintain design integrity in the PDF output\n- Set appropriate page sizes (A4, Letter, etc.) in the CSS using @page rules for consistent PDF rendering\n\n## Image Guidelines\n- ALWAYS use the Image Tool for image generation or image editing tasks\n- Write a single self-contained image prompt before calling the Image Tool\n- Clearly describe the main subject and overall composition\n- Explicitly specify the intended visual style and aesthetic\n- Provide exact text content if text is required; This blocks execution until user responds.\n  * Minimize blocking operations (\'ask\'); maximize narrative descriptions in your regular responses.\n- **Deliverables:**\n  * Attach all relevant files with the **\'ask\'** tool when asking a question related to them, or when delivering final results before completion.\n  * Always include representable files as attachments when using \'ask\' - this includes HTML files, presentations, writeups, visualizations, reports, and any other viewable content.\n  * For any created files that can be viewed or presented (such as index.html, slides, documents, charts, etc.), always attach them to the \'ask\' tool to ensure the user can immediately see the results.\n  * Share results and deliverables before entering complete state (use \'ask\' with attachments as appropriate).\n  * Ensure users have access to all necessary resources.\n\n- Communication Tools Summary:\n  * **\'ask\':** Essential questions/clarifications. BLOCKS execution. **USER CAN RESPOND.**\n  * **text via markdown format:** Frequent UI/progress updates. NON-BLOCKING. **USER CANNOT RESPOND.**\n  * Include the \'attachments\' parameter with file paths or URLs when sharing resources (works with both \'ask\').\n  * **\'complete\':** Only when ALL tasks are finished and verified. Terminates execution.\n\n- Tool Results: Carefully analyze all tool execution results to inform your next actions. **Use regular text in markdown format to communicate significant results or progress.**\n\n## 7.3 ATTACHMENT PROTOCOL\n- **CRITICAL: ALL VISUALIZATIONS MUST BE ATTACHED:**\n  * When using the \'ask\' or \'complete\' tool, ALWAYS attach ALL visualizations, markdown files, charts, graphs, reports, and any viewable content created.\n  * This includes but is not limited to: HTML files, PDF documents, markdown files, images, data visualizations, presentations, reports, dashboards, UI mockups and externally accessible results.\n  * NEVER mention a visualization or viewable content without attaching it\n  * If you\'ve created multiple visualizations, attach ALL of them\n  * Always make visualizations available to the user BEFORE marking tasks as complete\n  * For web applications or interactive content, always attach the main HTML file\n  * When creating data analysis results, charts must be attached, not just described\n  * Remember: If the user should SEE it, you must ATTACH it with the \'ask\' tool\n  * Verify that ALL visual outputs have been attached before proceeding\n\n- **Attachment Checklist:**\n  * Data visualizations (charts, graphs, plots)\n  * Web interfaces (HTML/CSS/JS files)\n  * Reports and documents (PDF, HTML)\n  * Presentation materials\n  * Images and diagrams\n  * Interactive dashboards\n  * Analysis results with visual components\n  * UI designs and mockups\n  * Any file intended for user viewing or interaction\n\n\n# 8. Core types for MCP protocol\n\nuse serde::{Deserialize, Serialize};\nuse std::collections::HashMap;\n\n/// MCP Tool - AI-callable security operation\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct Tool {\n    /// Unique tool identifier\n    pub name: String,\n    \n    /// Human-readable description\n    pub description: String,\n    \n    /// JSON Schema for input parameters\n    pub input_schema: serde_json::Value,\n    \n    /// Whether the tool requires authentication\n    pub requires_auth: bool,\n}\n\n/// Result of tool execution\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct ToolResult {\n    /// Success status\n    pub success: bool,\n    \n    /// Result data\n    pub data: Option<serde_json::Value>,\n    \n    /// Error message (if failed)\n    pub error: Option<String>,\n    \n    /// Additional metadata\n    pub metadata: HashMap<String, String>,\n}\n\nimpl ToolResult {\n    /// Create a successful result\n    pub fn success(data: serde_json::Value) -> Self {\n        Self {\n            success: true,\n            data: Some(data),\n            error: None,\n            metadata: HashMap::new(),\n        }\n    }\n    \n    /// Create a failed result\n    pub fn error(error: String) -> Self {\n        Self {\n            success: false,\n            data: None,\n            error: Some(error),\n            metadata: HashMap::new(),\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/// MCP Resource - Static documentation or reference\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct Resource {\n    /// Unique resource identifier\n    pub uri: String,\n    \n    /// Resource name\n    pub name: String,\n    \n    /// Description\n    pub description: String,\n    \n    /// MIME type\n    pub mime_type: String,\n    \n    /// Resource content\n    pub content: String,\n}\n\n/// MCP Prompt - Pre-built interaction pattern\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct Prompt {\n    /// Unique prompt identifier\n    pub name: String,\n    \n    /// Description\n    pub description: String,\n    \n    /// Prompt template\n    pub template: String,\n    \n    /// Required parameters\n    pub parameters: Vec<String>,\n}\n\n/// MCP Request\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct MCPRequest {\n    /// Request ID\n    pub id: String,\n    \n    /// Request method\n    pub method: String,\n    \n    /// Request parameters\n    pub params: serde_json::Value,\n}\n\n/// MCP Response\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct MCPResponse {\n    /// Request ID\n    pub id: String,\n    \n    /// Response data\n    pub result: Option<serde_json::Value>,\n    \n    /// Error (if any)\n    pub error: Option<String>,\n}\n\nimpl MCPResponse {\n    /// Create a successful response\n    pub fn success(id: String, result: serde_json::Value) -> Self {\n        Self {\n            id,\n            result: Some(result),\n            error: None,\n        }\n    }\n    \n    /// Create an error response\n    pub fn error(id: String, error: String) -> Self {\n        Self {\n            id,\n            result: None,\n            error: Some(error),\n        }\n    }\n}\n</create-file>\n</function_calls>'}

Sync>>>>;\n\n/// Trait that all tools must implement\n#[async_trait::async_trait]\npub trait ToolTrait: Send + Sync {\n    /// Get tool metadata\n    fn get_tool(&self) -> Tool;\n    \n    /// Execute the tool with given parameters\n    async fn execute(&self, params: serde_json::Value) -> MCPResult<ToolResult>;\n}\n\n/// Tool manager for registering and executing tools\npub struct ToolManager {\n    registry: ToolRegistry,\n}\n\nimpl ToolManager {\n    /// Create a new tool manager\n    pub fn new() -> Self {\n        Self {\n            registry: Arc::new(RwLock::new(HashMap::new())),\n        }\n    }\n    \n    /// Register a tool\n    pub async fn register<T>(&self, tool: T)\n    where\n        T: ToolTrait + Send + Sync + \'static,\n    {\n        let tool_info = tool.get_tool();\n        let name = tool_info.name.clone();\n        self.registry.write().await.insert(name, Box::new(tool));\n    }\n    \n    /// Get all registered tools\n    pub async fn list_tools(&self) -> Vec<Tool> {\n        self.registry\n            .read()\n            .await\n            .values()\n            .map(|tool| tool.get_tool())\n            .collect()\n    }\n    \n    /// Execute a tool by name\n    pub async fn execute_tool(&self, name: &str, params: serde_json::Value) -> MCPResult<ToolResult> {\n        let registry = self.registry.read().await;\n        \n        match registry.get(name) {\n            Some(tool) => tool.execute(params).await,\n            None => Err(MCPError::ToolNotFound(name.to_string())),\n        }\n    }\n    \n    /// Get a tool by name\n    pub async fn get_tool(&self, name: &str) -> MCPResult<Tool> {\n        let registry = self.registry.read().await;\n        \n        match registry.get(name) {\n            Some(tool) => Ok(tool.get_tool()),\n            None => Err(MCPError::ToolNotFound(name.to_string())),\n        }\n    }\n}\n\nimpl Default for ToolManager {\n    fn default() -> Self {\n        Self::new()\n    }\n}\n</create-file>\n</function_calls>'}

Tool manager\n    tool_manager: Arc<ToolManager>,\n    \n    /// Resources (static documentation)\n    resources: Arc<RwLock<Vec<Resource>>>,\n    \n    /// Running state\n    running: name.to_string(),\n            version: env!("CARGO_PKG_VERSION").to_string(),\n            tool_manager: Arc::new(ToolManager::new()),\n            resources: Arc::new(RwLock::new(Vec::new())),\n            running: Arc::new(RwLock::new(false)),\n        };\n        \n        // Register default tools\n        server.register_default_tools().await?;\n        \n        // Initialize default self.tool_manager.register(ThreatIntelTool).await;\n        \n        info!("Registered 4 default tools");\n        \n        Ok(())\n    }\n    \n    /// Initialize default resources\n    async fn         uri: "docs://api-reference".to_string(),\n            name: "V-Sentinel API Reference".to_string(),\n            description: "Complete API documentation for V-Sentinel security platform".to_string(),\n            mime_type: "text/markdown".to_string(),\n            content: include_str!("../resources/api_docs.md").to_string(),\n        });\n        \n        // Add FQL  });\n        \n        info!("Initialized 2 resources");\n        \n        Ok(())\n    }\n    \n    /// Handle MCP request\n    pub async fn handle_request(&self, request: MCPRequest) -> MCPResponse {\n        info!("Handling request: {} (id: {})", request.method, request.id);\n        \n        match request.method.as_str() {\n            "tools/list" => self.handle_list_tools(request).await,\n            "tools/call" => self.handle_tool_call(request).await,\n            "resources/list" => self.handle_list_resources(request).await,\n            "resources/read" => self.handle_read_resource(request).await,\n            "initialize" => self.handle_initialize(request).await,\n            _ => MCPResponse::error(\n                request.id,\n                format!("Unknown method: {}", request.method),\n            ),\n        }\n    }\n    \n    /// Handle tools/list request\n    async fn handle_list_tools(&self, request: MCPRequest) -> MCPResponse {\n        let tools = self.tool_manager.list_tools().await;\n        \n        MCPResponse::success(\n            request.id,\n            serde_json::json!({ "tools": tools }),\n        )\n    }\n    \n    /// Handle tools/call request\n    async fn handle_tool_call(&self, request: MCPRequest) -> MCPResponse {\n        let tool_name = request.params\n            .get("name")\n            .and_then(|v| v.as_str())\n            .unwrap_or("");\n        \n        let arguments = request.params\n            .get("arguments")\n            .cloned()\n            .unwrap_or(serde_json::json!({}));\n        \n        match self.tool_manager.execute_tool(tool_name, arguments).await {\n            Ok(result) => MCPResponse::success(\n                request.id,\n                serde_json::json!({ "result": result }),\n            ),\n            Err(e) => MCPResponse::error(request.id, e.to_string()),\n        }\n    }\n    \n    /// Handle resources/list request\n    async fn handle_list_resources(&self, request: MCPRequest) -> MCPResponse {\n        let resources = self.resources.read().await;\n        \n        let resource_list = resources\n            .iter()\n            .map(|r| serde_json::json!({\n                "uri": r.uri,\n                "name": r.name,\n                "description": r.description,\n                "mime_type": r.mime_type,\n            }))\n            .collect::<Vec<_>>();\n        \n        MCPResponse::success(\n            request.id,\n            serde_json::json!({ "resources": resource_list }),\n        )\n    }\n    \n    /// Handle resources/read request\n    async fn handle_read_resource(&self, request: MCPRequest) -> MCPResponse {\n        let uri = request.params\n            .get("uri")\n            .and_then(|v| v.as_str())\n            .unwrap_or("");\n        \n        let resources = self.resources.read().await;\n        \n        match resources.iter().find(|r| r.uri == uri) {\n            Some(resource) => MCPResponse::success(\n                request.id,\n                serde_json::json!({\n                    "contents": [{\n                        "uri": resource.uri,\n                        "mime_type": resource.mime_type,\n                        "text": resource.content,\n                    }]\n                }),\n            ),\n            None => MCPResponse::error(\n                request.id,\n                format!("Resource not found: {}", uri),\n            ),\n        }\n    }\n    \n    /// Handle initialize request\n    async fn handle_initialize(&self, request: MCPRequest) -> MCPResponse {\n        MCPResponse::success(\n            request.id,\n            serde_json::json!({\n                "protocolVersion": "2024-11-05",\n                "serverInfo": {\n                    "name": self.name,\n                    "version": self.version,\n                },\n                "capabilities": {\n                    "tools": {},\n                    "resources": {},\n                }\n            }),\n        )\n    }\n    \n    /// Start the server (marker for async transport implementations)\n    pub async fn start(&self) {\n        let mut running = self.running.write().await;\n        *running = true;\n        info!("MCP Server started");\n    }\n    \n    /// Stop the server\n    pub async fn stop(&self) {\n        let mut running = self.running.write().await;\n        *running = false;\n        info!("MCP Server stopped");\n    }\n    \n    /// Check if server is running\n    pub async fn is_running(&self) -> bool {\n        *self.running.read().await\n    }\n}\n</create-file>\n</function_calls>'}

Standard I/O transport for MCP server\n\nuse crate::error::MCPError;\nuse crate::server::MCPServer;\nuse crate::types::{MCPRequest, MCPResponse};\nuse crate::transport::Transport;\nuse async_trait::async_trait;\nuse std::io::{self, BufRead, Write};\nuse tokio::sync::RwLock;\nuse tracing::{info, error, debug};\n\n/// Standard I/O transport\npub struct StdioTransport {\n    server: std::sync::Arc<MCPServer>,\n    running: RwLock<bool>,\n}\n\nimpl StdioTransport {\n    /// Create a new stdio transport\n    pub fn new(server: std::sync::Arc<MCPServer>) -> Self {\n        Self {\n            server,\n            running: RwLock::new(false),\n        }\n    }\n    \n    /// Run the stdio transport\n    pub async fn run(&self) -> Result<(), MCPError> {\n        self.start().await?;\n        \n        let stdin = io::stdin();\n        let stdout = io::stdout();\n        let mut stdout_lock = stdout.lock();\n        \n        info!("Stdio transport started. Waiting for requests...");\n        \n        for line in stdin.lock().lines() {\n            match line {\n                Ok(json_line) => {\n                    debug!("Received: {}", json_line);\n                    \n                    // Parse request\n                    match serde_json::from_str::<MCPRequest>(&json_line) {\n                        Ok(request) => {\n                            // Handle request\n                            let response = self.server.handle_request(request).await;\n                            \n                            // Send response\n                            let response_json = serde_json::to_string(&response)\n                                .map_err(|e| MCPError::SerializationError(e))?;\n                            \n                            writeln!(stdout_lock, "{}", response_json)\n                                .map_err(|e| MCPError::IoError(e))?;\n                            \n                            debug!("Sent response");\n                        }\n                        Err(e) => {\n                            error!("Failed to parse request: {}", e);\n                        }\n                    }\n                }\n                Err(e) => {\n                    error!("Failed to read line: {}", e);\n                    break;\n                }\n            }\n            \n            if !*self.running.read().await {\n                break;\n            }\n        }\n        \n        info!("Stdio transport stopped");\n        Ok(())\n    }\n}\n\n#[async_trait]\nimpl Transport for StdioTransport {\n    async fn start(&self) -> Result<(), MCPError> {\n        let mut running = self.running.write().await;\n        *running = true;\n        self.server.start().await;\n        Ok(())\n    }\n    \n    async fn stop(&self) -> Result<(), MCPError> {\n        let mut running = self.running.write().await;\n        *running = false;\n        self.server.stop().await;\n        Ok(())\n    }\n    \n    fn is_running(&self) -> bool {\n        // Use blocking read for is_running\n        tokio::task::block_in_place(|| {\n            tokio::runtime::Handle::current().block_on(async {\n                *self.running.read().await\n            })\n        })\n    }\n}\n</create-file>\n</function_calls>'}

{'role': 'assistant', 'content': '<function_calls>\n<create-file file_path="/workspace/V-Sentinel/src/mcp/src/resources/api_docs.md">\n# V-Sentinel API Reference\n\nThis document provides comprehensive API documentation for the V-Sentinel security platform, designed for AI agents and developers.\n\n## Overview\n\nV-Sentinel provides a comprehensive RESTful API for interacting with all security capabilities, including threat detection, incident response, and threat intelligence.\n\n## Base URL\n\n```\nhttps://api.vsentinel.com/v1\n```\n\n## Authentication\n\nAll API requests require authentication using Bearer tokens:\n\n```\nAuthorization: Bearer <your_api_token>\n```\n\n## Rate Limiting\n\n- Standard: 1000 requests per minute\n- Premium: 5000 requests per minute\n\n## Endpoints\n\n### Detections\n\n#### Search Detections\n\n```\nGET /detections\n```\n\nQuery parameters:\n- `query` (string): FQL-style query\n- `time_range` (string): Time range (e.g., "1h", "24h", "7d")\n- `limit` (integer): Maximum results (default: 100, max: 1000)\n- `sort_by` (string): Sort field (default: "timestamp")\n\nExample:\n```bash\ncurl -H "Authorization: Bearer <token>" \\\n  "https://api.vsentinel.com/v1/detections?query=severity:critical&time_range=24h"\n```\n\nResponse:\n```json\n{\n  "detections": [\n    {\n      "id": "det_001",\n      "name": "Suspicious PowerShell Execution",\n      "severity": "critical",\n      "timestamp": "2026-03-06T10:30:00Z",\n      "host_id": "host_001",\n      "details": {\n        "process": "powershell.exe",\n        "command": "Invoke-Expression"\n      }\n    }\n  ],\n  "total": 1\n}\n```\n\n### Hosts\n\n#### List Hosts\n\n```\nGET /hosts\n```\n\nQuery parameters:\n- `host_id` (string): Specific host ID or hostname\n- `state` (string): Filter by state (online, offline, unknown)\n- `platform` (string): Filter by platform (Windows, Linux, macOS)\n\nExample:\n```bash\ncurl -H "Authorization: Bearer <token>" \\\n  "https://api.vsentinel.com/v1/host?state=online&platform=Windows"\n```\n\n### Incidents\n\n#### List Incidents\n\n```\nGET /incidents\n```\n\nQuery parameters:\n- `incident_id` (string): Specific incident ID\n- `severity` (string): Filter by severity (critical, high, medium, low)\n- `status` (string): Filter by status (new, in_progress, resolved, closed)\n- `limit` (integer): Maximum results (default: 50, max: 500)\n\n### Threat Intelligence\n\n#### Query Threat Intel\n\n```\nGET /threat-intel\n```\n\nQuery parameters:\n- `ioc` (string): Indicator of Compromise\n- `ioc_type` (string): Type (ip, domain, hash, url)\n- `threat_actor` (string): Threat actor name\n- `malware_family` (string): Malware family name\n\nExample:\n```bash\ncurl -H "Authorization: Bearer <token>" \\\n  "https://api.vsentinel.com/v1/threat-intel?ioc=192.168.1.100&ioc_type=ip"\n```\n\n## Error Codes\n\n| Code | Description |\n|------|-------------|\n| 400 | Bad Request |\n| 401 | Unauthorized |\n| 403 | Forbidden |\n| 404 | Not Found |\n| 429 | Rate Limit Exceeded |\n| 500 | Internal Server Error |\n\n## Webhooks\n\nV-Sentinel supports webhooks for real-time notifications:\n\n### Create Webhook\n\n```\nPOST /webhooks\n```\n\nRequest body:\n```json\n{\n  "url": "https://your-webhook-url.com",\n  "events": ["detection.created", "incident.updated"],\n  "secret": "your_webhook_secret"\n}\n```\n\n## SDKs\n\nOfficial SDKs are available for:\n- Python\n- Go\n- TypeScript/JavaScript\n- Rust\n\nSee the [V-Sentinel GitHub organization](https://github.com/vantisCorp) {'role': 'assistant', 'content': '<function_calls>\n<create-file file_path="/workspace/V-Sentinel/src/mcp/src/resources/fql_guide.md">\n# Falcon Query Language (FQL) Guide\n\nFQL (Falcon Query Language) is a powerful query language for searching and filtering security data in V-Sentinel.\n\n## Basic Syntax\n\nFQL uses a simple field:value syntax:\n\n```\nfield:value\n```\n\n## Supported Operators\n\n- `:` Equals\n- `!=` Not equals\n- `>` Greater than\n- `<` Less than\n- `>=` Greater than or equal\n- `<=` Less than or equal\n- `*` Wildcard\n- `~` Regex match\n\n## Common Fields\n\n### Detections\n\n| Field | Type | Description |\n|-------|------|-------------|\n| `severity` | string | Severity level (critical, high, medium, low) |\n| `status` | string | Detection status (new, in_progress, resolved) |\n| `hostname` | string | Host where detection occurred |\n| `filename` | string | Process filename |\n| `command_line` | string | Process command line |\n| `behaviors` | string | Detection behaviors |\n| `timestamp` | timestamp | Detection time |\n\n### Examples\n\n#### Search by severity\n```\nseverity:critical\n```\n\n#### Search by multiple severities\n```\nseverity:critical OR severity:high\n```\n\n#### Search by hostname\n```\nhostname:WORKSTATION-001\n```\n\n#### Search by process name\n```\nfilename:powershell.exe\n```\n\n#### Search by command line\n```\ncommand_line:*Invoke-Expression*\n```\n\n#### Search by behaviors\n```\nbehaviors:*\n```\n\n#### Search by time range\n```\ntimestamp:>2026-03-06T00:00:00Z\ntimestamp:<2026-03-07T00:00:00Z\n```\n\n#### Complex query\n```\nseverity:critical AND filename:powershell.exe AND command_line:*Invoke-Expression*\n```\n\n#### Wildcard search\n```\ncommand_line:*.exe\n```\n\n#### Regex search\n```\nhostname:~WORKSTATION-\\d+\n```\n\n## Logical Operators\n\nCombine multiple conditions with:\n\n- `AND` - All conditions must match\n- `OR` - Any condition must match\n- `NOT` - Condition must not match\n\n## Grouping\n\nUse parentheses to group conditions:\n\n```\n(severity:critical OR severity:high) AND hostname:WORKSTATION-*\n```\n\n## Time Range Syntax\n\nAbsolute time:\n```\ntimestamp:2026-03-06T10:00:00Z\n```\n\nRelative time:\n```\ntimestamp:>now-1h    # Last hour\ntimestamp:>now-24h   # Last 24 hours\ntimestamp:>now-7d    # Last 7 days\n```\n\n## Best Practices\n\n1. **Use specific fields** - More specific queries are faster\n2. **Avoid broad wildcards** - Use `*` only when necessary\n3. **Combine filters** - Use multiple conditions to narrow results\n4. **Use time ranges** - Always specify a time range when possible\n5. **Test queries** - Start with broad queries, then refine\n\n## Advanced Examples\n\n#### Critical detections in last hour on Windows hosts\n```\nseverity:critical AND timestamp:>now-1h AND platform:Windows\n```\n\n#### PowerShell with suspicious commands\n```\nfilename:powershell.exe AND (command_line:*Invoke-Expression* OR command_line:*DownloadString*)\n```\n\n#### Suspicious network activity\n```\nbehaviors:*network* AND (destination_ip:192.168.1.0/24 OR destination_ip:10.0.0.0/8)\n```\n\n#### Malware detections with specific behaviors\n```\nmalware:* AND (behaviors:*suspicious* OR behaviors:*malicious*)\n```\n\n## Performance Tips\n\n1. Index fields are faster: `severity`, `timestamp`, `hostname`\n2. Avoid leading wildcards: `*test` is slower than `test*`\n3. Use time ranges to limit results\n4. Limit result sets with `limit` parameter\n\n## MCP Integration\n\nWhen using FQL with the V-Sentinel MCP server tools:\n\n```json\n{\n  "name": "sentinel_search_detections",\n  "arguments": {\n    "query": "severity:critical AND timestamp:>now-24h",\n    "limit": 100,\n    "sort_by": "timestamp"\n  }\n}\n```\n\n## Troubleshooting\n\n### No results\n- Check field names are correct\n- Verify time range\n- Try broadening the query\n\n### Too many results\n- Add more specific filters\n- Reduce time range\n- Use `limit` parameter\n\n### Slow queries\n- Add time range\n- Use indexed fields\n- Avoid broad wildcards\n\n## Additional Resources\n\n- [V-Sentinel API Reference](docs://api-reference)\n- [MCP Tools Documentation](/docs/mcp-tools)\n- [FQL Examples](/examples/fql)\n</create-file>\n</function_calls>'}

AI-Callable Security Tools\n\n#### Detections Tool\n- **Name**: `sentinel_search_detections`\n- **Purpose**: Search and analyze security detections\n- **Parameters**:\n  - `query` (string): FQL-style query\n  - `time_range` (string): Time range (e.g., "1h", "24h", "7d")\n  - `limit` (integer): Maximum results (default: 100)\n  - `sort_by` (string): Sort field (default: "timestamp")\n\n#### Hosts Tool\n- **Name**: `sentinel_list_hosts`\n- **Purpose**: List and search hosts\n- **Parameters**:\n  - `host_id` (string): Specific host ID or hostname\n  - `state` (string): Filter by state (online, offline, unknown)\n  - `platform` (string): Filter by platform (Windows, Linux, macOS)\n\n#### Incidents Tool\n- **Name**: `sentinel_list_incidents`\n- **Purpose**: List and manage security incidents\n- **Parameters**:\n  - `incident_id` (string): Specific incident ID\n  - `severity` (string): Filter by severity (critical, high, medium, low)\n  - `status` (string): Filter by status (new, in_progress, resolved, closed)\n  - `limit` (integer): Maximum results (default: 50)\n\n#### Threat Intelligence Tool\n- **Name**: `sentinel_threat_intel`\n- **Purpose**: Query threat intelligence database\n- **Parameters**:\n  - `ioc` (string): Indicator of Compromise\n  - `ioc_type` (string): Type (ip, domain, hash, url)\n  - `threat_actor` (string): Threat actor name\n  - `malware_family` (string): Malware family name\n\n### 2. Static Resources\n\n#### API Documentation\n- **URI**: `docs://api-reference`\n- **Content**: Complete V-Sentinel API documentation\n- **Purpose**: AI agents can reference API endpoints and usage\n\n#### FQL Guide\n- **URI**: `docs://fql-guide`\n- **Content**: Comprehensive FQL query language guide\n- **Purpose**: AI agents can learn FQL syntax and best practices\n\n### 3. Transport Protocols\n\n#### Stdio Transport\n- Suitable for local development and testing\n- JSON-RPC over stdin/stdout\n- Easy to debug and test\n\n#### Planned Transports\n- SSE (Server-Sent Events): For real-time streaming\n- HTTP: For web-based integration\n\n## Usage\n\n### Starting the MCP Server\n\n```rust\nuse v_sentinel_mcp::MCPServer;\n\n#[tokio::main]\nasync fn main() -> Result<(), Box<dyn std::error::Error>> {\n    let server = MCPServer::new("V-Sentinel MCP Server").await?;\n    \n    // Start stdio transport\n    let transport = v_sentinel_mcp::transport::stdio::StdioTransport::new(\n        std::sync::Arc::new(server)\n    );\n    \n    transport.run().await?;\n    \n    Ok(())\n}\n```\n\n### Example Tool Call\n\n```json\n{\n  "jsonrpc": "2.0",\n  "id": "1",\n  "method": "tools/call",\n  "params": {\n    "name": "sentinel_search_detections",\n    "arguments": {\n      "query": "severity:critical AND timestamp:>now-24h",\n      "limit": 50,\n      "sort_by": "timestamp"\n    }\n  }\n}\n```\n\n### Response\n\n```json\n{\n  "jsonrpc": "2.0",\n  "id": "1",\n  "result": {\n    "result": {\n      "success": true,\n      "data": {\n        "detections": [\n          {\n            "id": "det_001",\n            "name": "Suspicious PowerShell Execution",\n            "severity": "critical",\n            "timestamp": "2026-03-06T10:30:00Z",\n            "host_id": "host_001",\n            "details": {\n              "process": "powershell.exe",\n              "command": "Invoke-Expression"\n            }\n          }\n        ],\n        "total": 1,\n        "query": "severity:critical AND timestamp:>now-24h",\n        "time_range": "24h"\n      },\n      "error": null,\n      "metadata": {}\n    }\n  }\n}\n```\n\n## Integration with AI Assistants\n\n### Claude (Anthropic)\n\nClaude can use the V-Sentinel MCP server to:\n- Search for security detections\n- Analyze threat intelligence\n- Respond to natural language queries\n- Automate incident investigation\n\n### Example Interaction\n\n**User**: "Find all critical detections from the last 24 hours"\n\n**Claude (using MCP)**:\n```json\n{\n  "name": "sentinel_search_detections",\n  "arguments": {\n    "query": "severity:critical",\n    "time_range": "24h",\n    "limit": 100\n  }\n}\n```\n\n**Response**: \n```\nI Malware Detection - MACBOOK-PRO-001 (8:20 AM)\n\nWould you like me to investigate any of these further?\n```\n\n## Benefits\n\n1. **AI-Driven Security Operations**: Automate threat hunting and incident response\n2. **Natural Language Interface**: Security analysts can use natural language\n3. **Reduced Workload**: Estimated 60-70% reduction in analyst workload\n4. **Faster Response**: Real-time threat intelligence and analysis\n5. **Consistency**: Standardized queries and responses\n\n## Future Enhancements\n\n1. **Additional Tools**:\n   - Container security tool\n   - Cloud security tool\n   - Network analysis tool\n   - Forensics tool\n\n2. **Advanced Features**:\n   - Multi-step workflows\n   - Automated remediation\n   - Threat hunting automation\n   - Incident response automation\n\n3. **Integration**:\n   - Claude (Anthropic) integration\n   - ChatGPT (OpenAI) integration\n   - Custom AI agent integration\n\n4. **Transport Protocols**:\n   - SSE implementation\n   - HTTP streaming\n   - WebSocket support\n\n## Testing\n\n### Unit Tests\n```bash\ncargo test --package v-sentinel-mcp\n```\n\n### Integration Tests\n```bash\ncargo test --package v-sentinel-mcp --features integration\n```\n\n### Manual Testing\n```bash\n# Start MCP server\ncargo run --package v-sentinel-mcp\n\n# Send test request\necho \'{"jsonrpc":"2.0","id":"1","method":"tools/list","params":{}}\' | \\\n  cargo run --package v-sentinel-mcp\n```\n\n## Documentation\n\n- [MCP Protocol Specification](https://modelcontextprotocol.io/)\n- [V-Sentinel API Reference](docs://api-reference)\n- [FQL Guide](docs://fql-guide)\n- [Competitive Analysis](../docs/COMPETITIVE_ANALYSIS_STRATEGY.md)\n\n## Contributing\n\nWhen adding new tools:\n1.
